ˌoː w ˈɑː t i ɑ , v ˈɛ s ə $dew. Modern Gheg vosë. De Rada has voesë. Old Tosk then *vaesë. Orel 1998(: 501). from ōvātium "...describing the falling dew as small eggs". May need to be reexamined. If it was Latin it would have to go from neuter to feminine, but given the fact that this is a mass noun in modern Albanian, it's trivially easy to see it coming from plural ovatia. It is not in Demiraj 1997 it seems. Not in Bonnet 1998. 
ˈoː w ɑ , v ˈɛ $egg. Attributed by Orel 2000(:37) as ovum to a late set of Latin loans with init o > Tosk va ~ Gheg vo (<ve). Alternatively, native, direct from PIE *h2ōwyóm "egg", per Huld 1984(ː125). May need to remove -- reexamine. Old Albanian vōe, Old Tosk *vae, Old Gheg voe (attested),Gheg vo, Shkoder vø, Arbëresh vö. Orel 1998: 497 -- who argues for Latin. Jokl 1923 reconstructies *ēu̯i̯ē. Most others including Cabej Huld Bopp Camarda etc attribute to Latin. De Vaan 1744 from ovā, going with that.

p ˌa e̯ n i t ˈeː n i oː , p ɛ n d ˈɔ j $verb: to regret, repent. As reflexive pendohem now. Vatasescu 1997: 464.

p ˌɑ ɡ ɑː t ˈuː r ɑ m , p a ɡ ə t ˈy ɾ ə $pay, wages (= pagë -- Newmark 1998(: 605) -- which is an Italian loan -- Dashi 2017(:313)). Suspected by Bonnet 1998(: 88, 317) to be a later formation and/or learned loan. May need to consider removal.

p ˈɑː n u s , p ˈɛ $thread. Orel 2000: 31, 56. pae ~ pê in Gheg. Orel has pānus, but note there was also pannus meaning garment. p ˌɑ r ˈɑ b o l ɑ , p ə r ˈa lˠ ə $fable, story. Orel 2000: 58, 112. Bonnet 384. Also përralloj < parabolare cf French parler? De Vaan 2017: 1740
p ˌɑ r ɑ d ˈiː s u s , p a r ˈi z $paradise. Orel 2000: 58. This etymology is disputed. Direct from Latin supported also by Orel 1998(:312), Miklosich, Tagliavini, Cabej, but Meyer suggests instead Italian paradiso; while Bonnet 1998(:17) instead supports Old Venetian paraíso while noting also Old French pareis. Marr 2023 supports an Angevin loan. Best bet may in fact be Old French pareis via the Angevin period (att. 1100--). Relevant oïl forsmː parais/parays (Anglo-Norman 1184--1300), paraïs/paraÿs (Anglo-Norman 1119--1251; Norman 1125 ; French 1150--1211), pareis ( French 1174-- 1200), pareïs (French 1100; Anglo-Norman 1100s; Norman 1227) , parëis (French 1150-1175; Picard 1200s). Matasovic 2024: 64.

pʰ ɑ s ˈe o l u s , f ɾ a ʃ ˈu a̯ lˠ $haricot. Gheg frashuell. -r- is secondary and epenthetic. Cabej St. I 175. Orel 1998: 102. Alas these forms do not seem to appear in Newmark (1998: 223). p ˈe k t e n , p ˈi t ɛ $honey-comb. Orel 1998(:328) -- "borrowed with phonetic irregularities... the immediate source must have been *pectum > *pejte..." Orel 2000(:117) gives the source form as pecten however. Unsure. (was there also a singularized plural here?) Reexamine. The nominative of Latin pecten is pecten, the accusative is pectinem, but pectinem would likely cause... further issues, as we don't see a form in -tër... Alas the Romance forms do seem to show that formː French peigne, Romanian pieptene & pieptǎn, Dalmatian piacno, Italian pettine, Sardinian petene & petiri... 
p ˌe k ˈu l i u m , p ɛ k ˈu l $personal wealth, precious friend; personal property to which an individual (and not family members) has right; property leased for high rent. Cabej 1962(: 180) apud Vatasescu. Phonological issues but semantically secure. Romanian dialectal picui, păcui; Aromanian picúl'iu, attributed as source of the Albanian by Puscariu, but this is less strong than Cabej's proposal. 
p ˈeː n s ɑ m , p ˈɛ ʃ ə $blubber, weight. Was neuter in Latin as pensum, pl. pensa. Reinterpreted as feminine? Singularized plural? May merit re-inspection... may also be derived from peshoj? Orel 2000(:115) has it from pensum. Bonnet 1998(: 62, 161, 225, 384) seems to also derive from pēnsum.

p l ˈɑ t ɑ n i ɑ , p ˈa l ɲ ə $maple. Other variantsː panjë, pënjë. Orel 1998: 309-10. Orel argues that another related form paltën (< Lat. platanus "plane-tree") is seen as Alb > Rom loanword paltin < x > Alb paltër, paltën. Çabej 1986(II: 9) instead treats this as a native cognate, Meyer 1891(:322) attributes it (or rather the forms without the /l/) to Str panj "stump". There are apparently a number of variants on this word.

p ˌo s ˈɑː n i oː , p u ʃ ˈɔ j $verb: to rest, vacation, cease, dismiss from duty. Posare not pausare as source per Topalli 2017: 1202. Bonnet 384 supports.
p ˈo s t e , p ˈɔ ʃ t ə $down, below, under. /ə/ inserted because adjective? Orel 2000: 27. Vatasescu 1997: 276, may be native perhaps but if so the phonology at this point is likely the same in what matters. Matasovic 2024: 66
p ˌo t e s t ˈɑː n i oː , p u ʃ t ˈɔ j $verb: to conquer. Orel 1998: 352. 
p ˌo t e s t ˈɑː t e m , p u ʃ t ˈɛ t $power. From accusative per Orel 1998: 352. Bonnet 384. 
p ˈo t t u s , p ˈɔ t $ mill-hopper, flour-bin, little boy. Orel 1998: 340. 
p r ˈa e̯ d ɑ , p r ɛ $prey, quarry. Feminine -- def form preja (Mario got it for me). Direct from Latin praeda ("plunder, war spoils, prey, game in hunt, profit") may regularly go to predhë however... Cf Romanian and Aromanian pradă. Possibly an Angevin (or Norman?) loan -- vvariation between preie and proie in Old French, preie holds on most in Old Northern French and Anglo-Norman preie "booty, bounty, prey". Modern French proie. More likely from Old French than Occitan -- Occitan has preda (Portuguese: preia, Spanish: prea) -- may be more likely "Norman" than "Angevin"...  Note that the doublet predhë actually exists. Orel 1998: 342. Bonnet 384/169. De Vaan 2017: 1734. 
p r ˈa e̯ d ɑ , p ɾ ˈɛ ð ə $missile, rocket. Doublet of the above. I suspect this is the regular one, and the above is a Norman or Angevin loan (cf. Marr 2023). Reexamine if necessary. 
p r ˌa e̯ d ˈɑː n i oː , p ɾ ˈu a̯ j $verb: to rob, to steal. Old Gheg -- in Bardhi as me pruem. Romanian a prăda. Vatasescu 1997: 374. 
p r ˌa e̯ ˈiː n i oː , p ɾ ˈi j $verb: to command. Lat inf praeīre. May be native, related to para.  Orel 1998: 345. Bonnet 384. Vatasescu 1997: 286. Matasovic 2024: 66
p r ˈa e̯ b y t e r , p ɾ ˈi f t $priest, pastor. Orel 2000(:27) argues it is a "later Latin" loan from presbyter. Topalli 2017 and Matzinger 2006 assert it's from a Vulgar Latin prepto: < praebitor, cf Romanian preot. This is supported by De Vaan 2017: 1744. Bonnet 1998(: 285) supports descent from a nominative praebyter; on loss of -r, he (p285) asserts survives in non-truncated stems such as the plural priftërinj, with the -n- in priftëria and (priftëreshë "wife of Pope" (semantics??!!)) being analogical in Gheg; note also Dalmatian (Vegliot) prat alongside pretro. 
p r ˈa e̯ b y t e r , p ɾ ˈi f t ə ɾ $priest, pastor. Testing Bonnet 1998's hypotheses. 
p r ˌiː m ɑ w ˈeː r ɑ m , p ɾ a n v ˈɛ ɾ ə $spring. Romanian primavara. Variants prëndverë, prandverë, prendverë, pramverë. In Buzuku, prandverë. Vatasescu 1997 p134, Mann 1934 p398, 400. 
p r ˈiː n k e s , p ɾ ˈi ɲ ɟ $chief, prince. A V Latin *prince(s) ultimately from princeps. Orel 1998: 346. Instead as prenk, prink in Vatasescu 1997(: 435) but none of these terms seem to be in Newmark 1998(: 689, 692). Reconsider? 
p r ˌiː w ˈɑː n i oː , p ɾ i v ˈɔ j $Verb: to rob. Orel 1998: 346. 
p r ˈiː w u m , p ɾ ˈɛ v ə $open way, track, road. Attributed to "another stage of contacts" in which Lat ī > Alb e per Orel 2000: 34. TODO reexamine, maybe remove (not in Bonnet 1998). Earlier authors noted in Orel 1998(: 344) equated it with trevë -- might it have been influenced by it? 
p r ˌoː d ˈɑː n i oː , p ɾ ɔ ð ˈɔ j $verb: to do good, produce. Orel 2000: 105. 
p r ˈo k s i m u s , p ɾ ˈɔ ʒ ə m $small wood, community forest. Older form: proshëm. Orel 1998: 347. 
p r ˌo k s i m ˈɑː n i oː , p ɾ ɔ ʒ m ˈɔ j $verb: to slander, libel. Compliccated semantic development -- Orel 1998: 347. Orel 2000: 119. Variant proshmoj. 
p r ˌoː m ˌi t t ˈo n i oː , p ɾ ɛ m t ˈɔ j $verb: to promise.  Orel 2000(ː32)-- among "the oldest Latin loanwords". Orel 1998: 343. On the other hand, Topalli 2017(:1182) attributes it to Italian promettere. Suggestion: this may actually be praemittere? 
p ˈuː b l i k ɑ , p ˈu k ə $promenade, public way, placename Pukë (region in northern Albania). Orel 1998: 348. Bonnet 1998: 88, 385. Vatasescu 1997: 338.
p ˈuː b l i k u s , p ˈu k $foolish. Orel 1998: 348. 
p ˈu l l ɑ m , p ˈu lˠ ə $chicken. May be < OF poule hence single l? But see also nulë < anulla, mulli < moli:num etc -- it's unnecessary. If from Old French, this would be an Angevin or Norman era loan. Occitan is not likely as it has /ʎ/ (which would render pujë) -- modern Occitan polhe, Catalan polla /poʎə/. Italian pollo also not a candidate, nor is Greek pouli. Orel 1998: 349. Bonnet 385. De Vaan 2017: 1735.
p ˈu l l u s , p ˈu l $"donkey's colt", or "foal". This form is unattested but it is the source of pulisht "donkey's coat". Orel 1998:  349. 
p ˈu l p ɑ m , p ˈu l p ə $pulp, calf of leg. Orel 1998: 349. 
p ˈu l w e r e m , b ˈu l b ə ɾ $street dust. Orel 2000: 104. 
p ˈu l w e r e m , p l ˈu h u ɾ $dust, powder. Vatasescu 1997 p138. 
p ˈu n ɡ ɑ m , p ˈu ŋ ɡ ə $purse, bag. A controversial etymology in Albanian as it is for Romanian pungă and Aromanian pungă. May be Latin (or later Latin), Germanic, perhaps via Latin, Greek... see Vatasescu 1997: 446 and sources therein. 
p ˈu n k t ɑ , p ˈu f t ə $empty, hollow. Only appears in the expression arrë puftë "empty nut" per Orel 1998(: 348), but metaphoric pejorative meanings for humans ('inept', 'empty-headed') noted in Newmark 1998(:699). Discussed as anomalous in Orel 2000:116. But couldn't this instead be from Romanian poftă "appetite" < pofti "to covet, crave" < Slavic *poxotěti ? 
p ˈu p p ɑ , p ˈu p ə $breast, teat, tassel, bud. Cf OFr poupe, Ital poppa. Duridanov to Thr *pupa. Derivation is pupërr "boil, furnacle". Orel 1998: 350. Bonnet 385.
p ˈu p p i s , p ˈu p ə $stern. Orel 1998: 350.

p ˈu t t ɑ n ɑ , p u t ˈə ɾ ə $whore. Gheg: putanë. Orel 1998: 352. Stress placement confirmed by native speakers.

r ˌɑ d ˈɑː n i oː , r ˈu a̯ j $scrape, shave. Matasovic 2024: 67.
r ˈɑ d i ɑ , r ˈɛ z ə $ray, spark, radius. Rr- not r-. Modern form is the singularized plural rreze, feminine. *rraz is not actually attested. Another attested variant: rrezë; per Bonnet: reze. Orel attributes to radius. Not rrez though -- so we go with Meyer deriving from Romance *radia. Bonnet 385. Now going with rrezë. Form "rreze" attested also in the Kuvendi i Arbënit (alas Old Gheg) -- Vatasescu 1997: 256. From plural? 
r ˌɑː d ˈiː k ɑ , r ˈi k ə $turnip. Orel 1998(:386) has source as Romance *rādica < Lat rādīx, reexamine. Bonnet 1998: 127, 242, 385. 
r ˌɑː d ˈiː k u l ɑ , r ˈi l k ə $turnip. Doublet of the above with metathesis of diminulative form. Orel 1998: 386; Bonnet 1998: 242. Long -iː- on basis of root even if not explicitly marked in a source. 
r ˈɑː m u s , r ˈɛ m b $branch. Orel 2000: 56. Distinct from reːmus > rrem "oar"? Gheg form of this is supposedly also ... rrem. Convalescence? Orel 1998: 380. Bonnet 385. 
r ˈɑː p ɑ , ɾ ˈa p ə $turnip. Orel 1998: 365. Related repë "radish" thought to be from Slavonic instead (Cabej 1970: 66 & Kristophson 1988: 87 apud Vatasescu 1997: 178). 
r ˈɑː p iː , r ˈɛ p $kale. Vatasescu 1997(:178) via Sejdiu 1979 (:254), V. lists rāpvm, plural inferred (proposed) here. Going with rrep for now. Forms also include repë and rrepë. 
r ˈɑː p u m , r a p $turnip, beet. Going with rrap. Modern form is rrepë, from the plural, but rrap attested in the Albanian of recent centuries. Attributed by some instead to Greek rhápus, PSlav *rěpa or natively from PAlb *(s)rˈāps. Orel 1998(:381) etc. 
r ˈɑː r u m , r ˈa lˠ ə $rare. Cf Spanish ralo. RALLVS "thin" may merit consideration? Orel 1998(ː377), Miklosich, Meyer, Jokl all attribute this to rallus. Maybe switch which form we're attributing this to? Bonnet 385. 
r ˈɑː s ɑ , ɾ ˈa ʃ ə $kind of woman's shirt. Feminized, Latin was rāsum. May have been borrowed from MLat - Orel 1998: 366. Confirmed as onset r-, not rr-. 
r ˌɑː s t ˈe l l u m , ɾ a ʃ c ˈɛ l $rake. Variant: rrashqel. Orel 1998: 366. Vatasescu 1997(: 348): Old Albanian (Gheg, Bardhi) rrashtjell. Form rashtjellë maz be a loan from Italian (Çabej 1976 t.I p.175 apud Vatasescu).
r ˌɑː t i ˈoː n e m , a ɾ s ˈy e̯ $reason. In Buzuku: masc arsye w. def sg. arseu, indef pl. arsenje. In Budi: arrësye. Orel thinks the o: > ye may be because it's after i -- Orel 2000: 34. Bonnet 385. De Vaan 2017: 1736 as arësye. In Buzuku and Bardhi -- arësye also -- Vatasescu 1997(: 68; she has the citation form also as arësye). Schumacher and Matzinger 2013(:224) attribute this to an arratiōnis (< ad-ratiōnem). 
r ˈeː b ɑ , r ˈɛ v ə $lot. Per Orel 1998(: 381), feminized of Latin rēbus, dat abl pl of rēs "thing, circumstance". TODO may merit reconsideration. 
r ˌe f ˈe r n i oː , r ə f ˈɛ j $verb: to tell. Orel 1998: 382; Meyer 1891: 373, Camarda 119; Çabej 1986(II: 93-4) prefers a prefixed Middle Greek loan. Lat inf. referre, 1sg. referō, 2sg refers etc, alas imperfect stem is -(r)ē-. Theme vowel treated as null. 
r ˈeː ɡ e m , ɾ ˈɛ ɟ $king. An exception in behavior of r per Orel 2000: 58. Orel 1998: 367. Suspected as a later, perhaps Italian loan, by Bonnet 1998(: 207-8) because of its onset /ɾ/ rather than /r/. Listed as Gheg, Arvanite and Arbereshe , and Old Gheg by Vatasescu 1997: 236, cf also Cabej 1982: 51. Derived regjëni in Bardhi -- Roques 114 apud Vatasescu p436. 
r ˈeː ɡ u l ɑ m , r ˈɛ ɡ u lˠ $rule (feminine, pl. rregulla). Orel 1998: 380. May instead come from Italian regola? -- cf. Bonnet 1998: 319, Dashi 2013: 368. May need to reexamine and reconsider.

r ˈeː t e , r j ˈɛ t ə $net. Alt form rrjet exists -- this may be the inherited one, with rrjetë with a final inserted ë as analogy because it is feminine. Orel 2000(:32) -- "presumably borrowed after the shift ē > EPA ā had taken place but before the diphthongization of short EPA *e, i.e. at the time when EPA *e was the best possible substitute for Lat ē".  Orel 1998: 388. Bonnet 385. 
r ˈeː s t e m , r j ˈɛ ʃ t $rank, line. Per Bonnet 1998(:385), following Jokl and Cabej 1986 II: 99-100, meanwhile Orel 1998:387-8, following Meyer 1891: 374, has it from regestum 'list', and notes the variant rresht. Going with Bonnet for now. 
r ˈeː t i n ɑ , r ˈɛ t ə ɾ $long leather rope, twisted leather lace. Gheg rretën. Variant retër ~ retën. Rom *retina "bridle" > cf French rêne. Orel 1998: 381. Also in Bonnet 1998 as rētina. Going with that for now (TODO may need to reconsider the length though).

r ˈoː b u r , r ˈɔ b u lˠ $Bosnian pine. Latin form meant English oak. Rr- not r-. "Most recent layer of Latin borrowings" per Orel 2000(:33). Orel 1998(:388) -- "dissimilation fo the sonorants". 
r ˈo k k ɑ , r ˈɔ k ə $spiral (from rucca ~ rocca "distaff" -- rocca seems most likely source if it is the same for Spanish rueca, cf also Ital rocca). Rr- not r-. Orel 1998: 389.
r ˌoː m ˈɑː n u s , ɾ ˈə m ə ɾ $Vlach, shephard, peasant. Gheg: rëmen. May be < rˈo:mɑ:nus, but Gheg form does seem to have second syll stress. Orel 2000: 58. Attested mainly in Greece. s ˈɑ l i k ɑ , ʃ ˈɛ l c ɛ $wooden vessel for salt, vessel used as plate by shepherds. Variants shelkë, sheqe. Shelkë also means "cover, wrapping". Reexamine. Orel 1998: 410.

s ˌɑ l i k ˈeː t u m , ʃ ɛ l c ˈɛ t $toponym in Zadrima, Shkoder county. Bonnet 323, 385
s ˌɑ l ˈiː n ɑ , ʃ ə lˠ ˈi ɾ ə $brine. Gheg and Old Gheg shëllinë. Vatasescu 1997 p91.
s ˌɑ l ˈiː n i oː , ʃ ə lˠ ˈi j $verb: to brine, to salt heavily. Orel 1998: 412. 
s ˌɑ l w ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ ə l b ˈɔ j $verb: to bring salvation, liberate. Orel 2000: 110. Orel 1998: 412. Vatasescu 1997: 436. 
s ˌɑ l w ˈɑː n t i ɑ , ʃ ə l b ˈɛ s ə $salvation. Proposed by Vatasescu 1997(: 436) as from Lat salvātiō, this here is another PROPOSAL. 
s ˌɑ l w i ˈe l l ɑ , ʃ ɛ ɾ b ˈɛ l ə $sage. Orel 1998: 411. Topalli 2017: 1378. Source for salviella also supported in Vatasescu 1997(:183) without explicating reflex, citing Cabej 1962: 197, 1964, 3: 29. Bonnet 1998(: 55) has doubts however, and (p. 275) floats *salviola and influence from sherp "celery". 
s ˌɑː n ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ ə ɾ ˈɔ j $verb: to heal, repair. Orel 1998: 413. Bonnet 386. Bonnet 1998(:181-2) attributes the Gheg form shëroj to a Tosk loan, influenced also by pressure to distinguish it from shënoj (ultimately, < SIGNĀRE) "to mark", which can also mean "to scar". 
s ˌɑː n i t ˈɑː t e m , ʃ ə n d ˈɛ t $health, greeting, "bless you". Orel 1998: 412. De Vaan 2017: 1735 as sa:nitta:tem. Bonnet 386 as from sānitās (acc -tātem, ofc.). 
s ˌɑː n i t ˈoː s u s , ʃ ə n d ˈɔ ʃ ə $able-bodied, fit (but also: chubby?). Final /ə/ likely just because it's an adjective. Many sources list it as coming from sanitosus (masc form), though this is probably a moot point. Gheg: shnosh (Old Gheg: "scnnosc"). "Most recent layer of Latin borrowings" per Orel 2000(:33). Orel 1998: 413. De Vaan 2017: 1735 as "healthy". Bonnet 386 as "bien pourtant". 
s ˌɑ n ɡ u i n i ˈɑː t ɑ , ʃ ə ɲ ɟ ˈɛ t ə $best part of hunted animal. Matasovic 2024: 67. 
s ˌɑ n ɡ u i s ˈu n ɡ i ɑ , ʃ u ʃ ˈu ɲ ə $leech. Topalli 2017: 1438; Orel 1998: 447; Orel 2000: 103. Latin in "bloodsucker" + a nominalization of "suck". See however ushenjëz which seems to very possibly be native, and possibly related... but otherwise, Romance cognates in Dalmatian sansoike, Sicilian sancisuca (?), Friulian sansuie/sansuje, Piedmontese sansu(v)a, Franco-Provencal sangsua (Valdotain sang-suva), French sangsue, Occitan sangsuga, Aragonese sansuga, Galician sam(b)esuga, Spanish sanguja , Sardinian sambesuca. Vatasescu(p222) treats the input as -sungia but maybe try with -sugia too? 
s ˌɑ n k t ɑ m t r ˌiː n i t ˈɑː t e m , ʃ ə n d ə ɾ t ˈa t $Transfiguration, Trinity (why not -tet?). Orel 1998: 413. In Budi, Shendritat -- Bonnet 1998(48, 263). Also in Old Albanian -- "e shendë Teritat" (Vatasescu 1997 p470).
s ˈɑː n k t u s , ʃ ˈɛ ɲ t ə $sacred, saint. Final /ə/ likely just because it's an adjective? Orel 2000: 117. De Vaan 2017: 1745 as "holy". Vatasescu 1997: 470 -- Old Gheg shint (Bardhi), shënëndre "November (Saint Andrew?)" (Bogdani), dialectal Shëmëhill "Saint Michael, November", shëmiter "October" (= Romanian sâmedru), and Toponyms Shëngjin (Saint John -- Sanctus Ioannes? or Gentius), Shënkoll (Saint Nicolas), Shën Vlash (Saint Vlasius (???)), Shijak (Saint Jacob -- Sanctus Iacobus), kelshêjt "the holy chalice" < CALICEM SANCTUM. -- TODO incorpoirate these? 
s ˌɑ p p ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ a p ˈɔ j $verb: to polish. Orel 1998: 408. Cf Romanian sapă, Italian zappa. 
s ˈɑ p u m , ʃ a p $alum. Latin was sapa, feminine, but form loaned seems neuter or masc? Orel 1998: 407. 
s ˈɑ r i k ɑ m , ʃ ˈa ɾ k ə $clothes of white wool. Romanian sarică. Vatasescu 1998: 81. 
s ˌɑ r k i n ˈɑː r i u s , ʃ ɛ l c ə ɾ ˈu a̯ ɾ $trunk with several branches used as a hanger in front of a shepherd's hut. Actual attested Tosk is shelqëror. Gheg: shelqnuer, shelknuer. As of June 2024, using shelqëruar as presumed Old Tosk form before analogy off of the definite (cf. kalor-i) happened(?). Cf Romanian sărciner, sălciner. Reexamine. Orel 1998: 410. Vătășescu 1997: 392. 
s ˌɑ r m ˈe n t u m , ʃ ə ɾ m ˈɛ n d $grape shoot.  Orel 1998: 411 as shermend. Bonnet 386 has it as  sharmend, whereas he has shërmend on p339; all of these seem to be variant forms; on p54 Bonnet contrasts a Tosk shërmend from a Gheg shermênn. Decide which to use (consult Newmark?). 
s ˌɑ t ˈu r n iː , ʃ t ˈu n ə $Saturday. May need revision. Final schwa because adjective? Orel 1998(:444) attributes it to saturni̍ diēs contraction, notes early form shëtundë in Buzuku and Bardh. Bonnet 1998(: 392) as an "uncertain" Latin etymology. Bonnet 1998(: 213) suggests homophony avoidance of sorts from shturrë "starling" (> modern shturë? Newmark 1998). Reexamine? Per Vatasescu p131: Old Albnaian të shëtundë in Buzuku, Tosk shëtunë; Cabej 1982 (p118 apud Vatasescu) "considers it a late loan without arguing afirmatively" 
s ˌe k r ˈeː t u s , ʃ k ɾ ˈɛ t ə $deserted, lonely, dead, wretched, unplowed. Cf Romanian săcret, same semantic evolution. Orel 1998: 423. Bonnet 62, 221, 341, 386. 
s ˈe k t ɑ , ʃ ˈa t ə $"bran". Now only exists as its plural, shete. Double case of singularized plural, Latin was og neuter sectum. Note that it is secta not sectum that is inherited in Italian setta, Portuguese seita. Orel l998: 412... 
s ˈe k t u m , ʃ ˈa t $hoe. Pl. shata or shetër. Orel 2000: 26 -- Orel argues sector is the ancestor. Orel 1998: 409. Demiraj 1997 argues it is a native PAlb sakta however. Reexamine?
s ˌe k w ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ i k ˈɔ j $look. Matasovic 2024: 67. 
s ˈe l l ɑ , ʃ ˈa l ə $saddle, inner thigh. Orel 2000: 26. Cf Romanian șale. Orel 1998: 407. De Vaan 2017: 1735. Cabej 1962 disputed, 1966 accepted the Latin etymology, apud Vatasescu 1997 p337. 
s ˈe n s ɑ , ʃ ˈi s ə $feeling. Dissimilated from *shishë. Matasovic 2024: 67. Consider possibility of native etymology and relation to shije. 
s ˈe r r ɑ , ʃ ˈa r ə $saw. Orel 2000: 26. May be from Aromanian shară. Orel 1998:409. De Vaan 2017: 1735.
s ˌe r t ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ a ɾ t ˈɔ j $verb: to crossbreed. < Vulg Lat *sertō. Orel 1998: 408-9. Bonnet 386. 
s ˌe r w ˈiː n i oː , ʃ ə ɾ b ˈɛ j $verb: to serve. Orel 2000: 110. Orel 1998: 413. De Vaan 2017: 1743. 
s ˌe r w ˈi t i u m , ʃ ə ɾ b ˈɛ s $service. De Vaan 2017: 1735. Bonnet 386 as shërbesë, but in index as shërbes and also elsewhere. Cf Bonnet 1998: 65, 156, 237, 303. Listed as shërbes in Newmark's dictionary. Hamp 1973 (in Bonnet) proposed that shërbes was a secondary blend of shërbesë and *shërbis, while Çabej 1973 preferred a formation of shërbes in parallel to mallëkes (all in Bonnet).Bardhi me shërbuem, and Buyuku has sherbëtyrë already (see below.), there is also a shërbesë perhpas from the lpl. servitia -- all from Vatasescu 1997(: 437-8) and sources therein. 
s ˌe r w iː t ˈoː r e m , ʃ ə ɾ b ə t ˈɔ ɾ $servant. Cabej 1982: 117. May be present in Bardhi, Old Gheg, as sherbëtuer -- Roques p150 apud Vatasescu 1997(: 437). 
s ˌe r w iː t ˈuː r ɑ m , ʃ ə ɾ b ə t ˈy ɾ ə $service. Bonnet 1998(:88, 317) -- possibly a later formation based on shërbej and -tyrë, and/or a sort of learned loan. Consider removal. Vatasescu 1997: 437 -- as already in Buzuku. 
s ˈe s s u s , ʃ ˈɛ ʃ $plane, floor, ground square (in a city). Orel 2000: 25. Bonnet 1998: 54, 59. Form listed in p386 of the latter is plural but this seems unproblematic based on description elsewhere and otherwise. 
s ˌi ɡ n ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ ə n ˈɔ j $verb: to sign, mark, note, score. May need further inspection (reexamine) -- acknowledged in Bonnet 1998(:182) but merely as related to shenjë (< SIGNVM). Also Vatasescu 1998: 322, as shenjoj.
s ˈi ɡ n u m , ʃ ˈɛ ɲ ə $mark, notch, scar, birthmark, trace, (shooting) target (on meanings -- Bonnet 1998(:187), Newmark 1998: 798-9). Orel 2000(:28-9) attributes it to "later layer of Latin loanwords" when short e reappeared but an "older" layer for ɡn >nj  (ː115). Endorsed by De Vaan 2017: 1740, citing Bonnet 1998(:187-8) on role of INSIGNIA and SIGNVM. Bonnet 1998: 65, 187-8; Mihaescu 1993: 42, 46. Actually shenjë̈in the modern day, apparently due to influence from shenjë < INSIGNIA (Bonnet 1998: 188). In Buzuku as shenj, in the neuter, which can be seen as regular in his Gheg as well it seems (?) (Bonnet 1998: 188). For if the sheng cited by Meyer 1895(:71) was in fact the regular outcome, another entry is added below to handle this possibility for now. Alas, also possibly a Venetian (Bonnet 1998: 221) or Italian (Helbig 1904:75) loan, apparently? 
s ˈi ɡ n u m , ʃ ˈɛ ŋ $mark, notch, scar, birthmark, trace, (shooting) target-- alternate possibility for the above ~ cf. Bonnet 1998(:187-8); Mihaescu 1993(:42, 46), Meyer 1895(:71). Me note (TODO): there is also Latin īnsigne (nom & acc) "distinguishing mark, emblem, badge, ensign, coat of arms".  
s ˈiː k , ʃ ˈi $exactly, right (adv). Orel 1998: 414. Perhaps slightly later from Migration Age Italo-Romance or Dalmatian? Matasovic 2024: 68.
s ˈi k l ɑ , ʃ ˈɛ c ə $large wooden vessel. Now shekë, by backformation of new singular with *sheqë interpreted as plural -- Orel 1998: 409. De Vaan 2017: 1743 as meaning "sickle", from Lat sitla > sicula > sicla. Reexamine? Cf also Vatasecu 1997 (:400) noting the shekle in Buzuku also noted in Çabej 1982(: 37). Originally form a situla, but sicla is panromanic for Vatasescu (with the exception of Romanian). 
s ˈi k u l ɑ , ʃ ˈi k ə lˠ $gall-nut. Romance *sicla < Lat silicula "small pod". Orel 1998: 414. Later loan? May need to reexamine. 
s ˌi m i l ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ ə m b ə lˠ ˈɛ j $verb: to resemble. Orel 2000: 56. Matasovic 2024: 68.
s ˌi m i l ɑ t ˈuː r ɑ , ʃ ə m b ə lˠ t ˈy ɾ ə $image. Suspected by Bonnet 1998(:88, 317) to be a learned loan and/or later formation; consider removing.
s ˈiː n u s , ʃ ˈi $occiput. Gheg only, as shî. Orel 1998: 414. But source of shibë which also exists in Tosk. 
s ˈi r p e , ʃ ˈɛ ɾ p $celery. Topalli 2017: 1409, Vatasescu 1997: 185. 
s ˈi t ɑ , ʃ ˈi t ə $illness affecting sheep. From Latin situs, analogized to a final -a because it's feminine/feminized? Latin  seems to be the situs that is "decay, rust, filthiness in body", with genitive sitūs. Orel 1998: 415.  May be dubious, unclear. 
s k ˈɑ b i eː s , z ɟ ˈɛ b ɛ $itch, scab. May need to reexamine. Orel 1998: 523. Vatasescu 1997: 77. Relevant for theory that sk > zgj under i-mutation, suggesting i-mutation was realized in a yod that was moved backwards.
s k ˈɑː l ɑː , ʃ k ˈa l ə $stairs. Orel 2000(:30) has it from a plural scālae, but there is no reason not to have scāla as Bonnet 1998(:392) does phonologically.
s k ˈɑ m n u m , ʃ k ˈə m b $cliff, chair, throne. Gheg shkamb. Orel 2000: 114. Orel 1998: 420. De Vaan 2017: 1741 as "rock". Bonnet 386.  Old Albanian shkamn also attested. = Romanian scaun. Vatasescu 1997: 437. 
s k ˈɑ n d u l u m , ʃ k ˈa n d u lˠ $temptation. Orel 1998: 417.
s k i ˈe n t i ɑ , ʃ k ˈɛ n t͡s ə $science. Orel 1998: 419. May need to revisit this one. May be medieval learned Latin loan; may need to reconsider. Not in Bonnet 1998 nor Dashi 2017. Matasovic 2024: 66.
s k ˌi n t ˈi l i ɑ , ʃ k ə n d ˈi j ə $spark, twinkle, firefly. Cf Romanian scânteie. Orel 2000: 109. Orel 1998: 420.
s k l ˈɑ w u m , ʃ c ˈa $Serb, or (per Orel) Bulgarian. Pejorative. Orel 2000: 55. Orel 1998: 432. "Slav" per De Vaan 2017: 1741. Vatasescu 1997(: 437): plural shqe; in Mandrica, Albanian village in Bulgaria it is shkla (in sg.) and pl. shkle; Old Gheg Shqeni "Slavonia", = Old Tosk Shqeri, from the plural shqe. 
s k l ˈoː p u s , ʃ c ˈɛ p $lame. Now shqepoj -- verb: to be lame. But shqep adj is attested. Orel 1998: 433. Orel 2000: 113. De Vaan 2017: 1741 as excloppus. Reexamine? 
s k ˈo d r ɑ , ʃ k ˈɔ d ə ɾ $Shkodër. Curtis 2012: 17. 
s kʰ ˈo l ɑ , ʃ k ˈɔ lˠ ə $school. Old Alb: "scollë" (Arb~sh). Orel 1998: 421. Date of loaning not quite clear. See Vatasescu 1997: 488, may be a similar case with (and even linked with) LIBER > libër, per Haarmann 1977(: 321, apud Vățășescu 1997: 488), who rejects the idea of more recent Italian loaning.  
s k ˈoː p ɑ , ʃ c ˈɔ p ə $heather, heath, briar. This one is suspicious -- re-examine. On  the /ɔ/ː "Most recent layer of Latin borrowings" per Orel 2000(:33). But why /c/? Orel 1998(ː434) calls it secondary. Reexamine.
s k ˌo p ˈeː t u m , ʃ k ɔ p ˈɛ t $toponym, Zadrima, Shkoder county. Attested as Scopetum in medieval Latin. Du Cange 1678, apud Bonnet 1998: 324. Bonnet argues against Cabej's use of scōpae as the Latin hypothesis for this item (to argue against), instead preferring scopa, referring a plant favoring rocky places, for geobotanical reasons. 
s k ˈoː r i ɑ , z ɟ ˈy ɾ ə $rust. Suspicious but cf Orel 2000(:33) on the /y/. Re-examine. Orel 1998: 524. Romanian scoare (with scorie being a loan?) alongside zgura -- see discussion in Vatasescu 1997: 395. Relevant for theory that sk > zgj under i-mutation, suggesting i-mutation was realized in a yod that was moved backwards.
s k ˈo r t e ɑ , ʃ k ˈɔ ɾ s ə $rug made of goat wool. Orel 1998: 422. Bonnet 1998: 386.
s k r ˌiː b ˈo n i oː , ʃ k ɾ ˈu a̯ j $verb: to write. Disputed. Orel 1998: 423. Lat infinitive was scrīběre. But may be native. See discussion in Vatasescu 1997: 488-9.
s k ˈu l k ɑ m , ʃ k ˈu l k ə $"barked willow branch stuck in the middle a meadow to show that the land, being occupied, cannot be use for grazing; after mowing, the branch is removed". Vatasescu 1997: 381. May come from Gothic. Mihaescu 1993(:474) asserts a later date on the assumption that the Latin form had -ū-, but a short -ǔ- instead seems evident in Italian scolca. Although only shkulkë is in Newmark 1998(: 814, 819), also noted (forms and definitions in Vatasescu) have been shkojkë "ramură indicând ocuparea  unei pajişti; strajă, pază" and a Gheg form shkujkë; Çabej apud Vatasescu considered the Gheg form to be older and wondered about Byzantine influence on it, a proposal not favored by Mihaescu (all apud Vatasescu). The form is widespread in Western Romance, but is absent in Balkan Romance (REW number 7753). Possibly native? 
s k ˈu m ɑ , ʃ k ˈu m ə $foam. Likely ultimately Germanic. Variant: shkumbë. Orel 1998: 424. 
s k r ˌuː t ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ c y ɾ t ˈɔ j $verb: to examine, observe. Meyer has it from Romance *disquiritare, as does Vatasescu 1997(:66), noting Old Gheg çqyrëtinj. Cabej derives it from qyr. Orel argues for an original unattested shkrytoj. Orel 1998: 435. Lat def scrūtārī
s k ˈuː t u m , ʃ c ˈy t $shield, coat-of-arms. Modern variant sqyt? Orel 1998: 401; explicitly lists shqyt (separately!) on p435. Bonnet 88, 386. 
s k w ˈɑː t u s , ʃ k ˈa t $ray, skate. Form unattested. Attested as shkatërr, result of suffixation. Orel 1998: 418. 
s l ˈu k u s , ʃ l ˈu k $blister. Metathesis sulcus > slucus prior to borrowing per Orel 1998(:425).
s ˈo k ɑ , ʃ ˈɔ k ə $belt. Cf French soue, Ital dial. soga etc. Orel 199*: 426. Bonnet 386 as "woman's belt". Vatasescu 85. 
s ˈo k i ɑ , ʃ ˈɔ c ɛ $female friend, girlfriend. Bonnet 1998: 148.
s ˈo k i u s , ʃ ˈɔ c $male friend, comrade, boyfriend. Modern singular shok is hypersingular form after inherited sg shoq reinterpreted as plural. Orel 1998: 426. De Vaan 2017: 1735 as shok. 
s ˈo l ɑ , ʃ ˈɔ lˠ ə $sole. Variant shuallë. Feminized(?) from Lat solum. Orel 1998: 426. 
s ˌo l ˈɑː n u s , ʃ ˈu lˠ ə $sunny spot. Gheg shullâ̂ appears to show regular behavior, unclear what's going on here in Tosk. Orel 2000: 109 on analogy.  Orel 1998: 445. Pl. shullëri, in Gheg shullani. Vatasescu 146. 
s ˈo l u m , ʃ ˈu a̯ lˠ $sole. De Vaan 2017: 1736. Vatasescu 1997: 37. 
s ˈo l ɑ , ʃ ˈɔ lˠ ə $sole, form plural (?). Matasovic 2024: 68. 
s ˈo r b ɑ , ʃ ˈu ɾ b ə $service tree. Doublet survë < Greek sourvia < also Latin sorbum. Topalli 2017: 237. Latin was sorbum but apparently feminized in Albanian and Greek alike. Vatasescu 1997(: 172), citing Haarmann 1972 (: 42) and Sejdiu 1984 (: 228), identifies this as an Arbereshe idiom and suggests that this is from a plural SORBA of a SORBVM "fructul sorbului, scorușă". Bonnet 1998(ː78) does list shurb however. 
s ˈo r t e m , ʃ ˈɔ ɾ t $lot, sweepstakes. Orel 1998: 426-7. Matasovic 2024: 68
s ˌo r t ˈiː k ɑ , ʃ ɔ ɾ t ˈɛ k ə $hole of honeycomb. Via unattested *shortekë, now shoretkë. Attributed to "another stage of contacts" in which Lat ī > Alb e per Orel 2000: 34. Reexamine. Orel 1998: 426.
s ˌo r t ˈi l e ɡ iː , ʃ ˈɛ r ə ɟ $spell, poison, deceit, bewitchment. Later suffixed in öi. Old Alb. sherregji ,sherragjuer, sherrgjuer. See Vatasescu 1997: 484. 
s p ˈɑ tʰ ɑ m , ʃ p ˈa t ə $sword. Orel 1998: 428. Bonnet 1998: 386. 
s p ˈɑ r t ɑ , ʃ p ˈa ɾ t ə $broom (botany). Lat spartum, feminized? Orel 1998: 428. Matasovic 2024: 68.
s p ˈɑ tʰ u l ɑ , ʃ p ˈa t u lˠ $shoulder. (final schwa lost?  still fem though fpl shpatulla). Orel 1998: 428. Vatasescu 1997: 32.
s p ˈeː l a e̯ ɑ , ʃ p ˈɛ lˠ ə $cave. Lat spēlaeum, feminized (via *spēla?). Orel 1998: 428-9. 
s p ˌe r ˈɑ n t i ɑ , ʃ p ɾ ˈɛ s ə $hope. Vătășescu 1997: 60, citing Kristophson 1988 (:78). Cf. inherited Sp. esperanza, Ital. speranza, Old Occ esperanssa > Occ. esperança, etc..., and also apparently Dalmatian. Possible lack of nasal in Gheg may be issue unless it's a loan from Tosk. Orel 1998(:431) instead considers it derived from shp(ë)rej; Bonnet 1998(:304) seems to accept this with reservations. Other etymologies (unsourced?) online think it is a native formation. 
s p ˌeː r ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ p ə ɾ ˈɛ j $verb: to hope. Orel 1998: 431; Bonnet 1998: 286, 303-304, 386. Meyer 1891: 414. Matasovic 2024: 68. 
s p ˈiː n ɑ , ʃ p ˈi n ə $spine, back, top part, backrest, rear. Orel 1998: 430. Vatasescu 1997: 32.
s p ˌiː r ˈɑː n i oː , ʃ p i r ˈɔ j $unattested source of deverbal shpirrë "asthma". May instead be from a Vulgar Latin dis-spīrāre -- as per Orel 1998: 430. TODO reexamine. Does not seem to be in Bonnet 1998. Vatasescu 1998ː 41. 
s p ˈiː r i t u s , ʃ p ˈi ɾ t $soul, spirit. Orel 1998: 430. 
s p ˈi s s u s , ʃ p ˈɛ ʃ ə $thick. Final schwa because adjective? Orel 1998: 429. 
s p ˈi s s u s , ʃ p ˈɛ ʃ $often. Cf Italian spesso, Aromanian spes. Bonnet 1998: 341 -- adjectival form i shpeshtë "frequent; dense" (on latter cf. "thick" meaning above.). 
s p l ˌe n ˈe t i k u m , ʃ p ɾ ˈɛ t k ə $spleen.  Orel 2000: 31. Bonnet 1998: 386. Vatasescu 1997: 32 ~ Tosk shp(ë)retkë and Gheg shp(ë)netkë
s p ˈo d i u m , ʃ p ˈu z ə $embers, hot ash. "Early" Latin per Orel 2000: 28. Bonnet 1998: 386. 
s p ˈo r t ɑ , ʃ p ˈɔ ɾ t ə $basket. Orel 1998: 431. Vatasescu 1997: 401. 
s t ˈɑ b u l u m , ʃ t ˈa lˠ ə $stall. Orel 2000: 119.Orel 1998: 436.
s t ˈɑ m n u m , ʃ t ˈa m $tin. Mostly Gheg. Old Albanian also has shtambje. Vatasescu 1997 p141, Mann 1948 p497.

t ˌe r e b ˈe l l u m , t u ɾ j ˈɛ l ə $drill. Orel 2000:58? Bonnet 1998(: 136): variants in turjellë, trellë, and trujellë also exist; Bonnet argues trellë is essentially a clipping of turjellë, and suspects trujellë to be a reflex of Venetian truelo. Pedersen 1895(: 539, cited in Bonnet p136) disputes this Latin etymology, which was first posited by Meyer 1891(: 542), preferring (Tuscan) Italian trivello. Bonnet entertains the possibility that turjellë is a variant from of trujellë (< Ven. truelo) and that turjelë saw a change in -l- under *later* Italian (trivello) influence.

t ˌiː m ˈoː n e m , t i m ˈu a̯ $wheel of a ship. Only in Gheg as timue, def. form timoni. Classical Latin was tēmō, tēmōnis, but tīmo- forms were inherited in Sardinina, Venetian, Catalan, French, Occitan, Asturian, Portuguese, Spanish (temo- forms in Friulian, Lombard and Romansch only). Romanian timona is a later loan, some think this is too. See Vatasescu 1997: 338, and cited Mihaescu 1981 & 1993; Kristophson 1988 (:87) as sceptic. 
t ˌi m ˈoː r e m , t m ˈɛ r $dread, horror. Jokl, Çabej etc think it is native, but the timo:rem case wfrom Orel (1998: 458) seems best here. Various regional variants exist: mer, kmer, kmerrë, mner, mnerë, tmerrë.  Orel 2000(ː32)-- among "the oldest Latin loanwords". See also Orel 2000: 58.

t ˈo r k u l u m , t ˈɔ ɾ k u lˠ $"wooden olive press", variant forms are torkull and trokull, both feminine (Newmark 1998: 871, 879). I propose torkull as the etymological form and trokull as metathesized, from Latin torculum "olive press, wine press" (REW 8792a, p666). This is thus a doublet of tork "trough used for crushing  grapes", an analogical singular of a loan from Italian torchio (Orel 1998: 460).

w ˌɑ l ˈɑː n i oː ,  v l ˈɛ j $verb: to be worth. Identical to vjej "to need"? Orel 1998: 512. Orel doesn't consider them equivalent, but does note the variants vëjej and vjej... maybe the two diverge because of the semantic distinction? Likewise Bonnet 387. TODO reconsider... Vatasescu 1997(: 68)-- Old Alb had vëlej for this and vëjej for "to need". PROPOSAL: changed this from valēre (equivalent to vëjej) to valāre, on the basis of Vegliot Dalmatian valar, Romansch valair (REW number 9130). Bonnet 1998(: 203) notes Buzuku's "vœglièn" for "vlen", generally a word of perlexion for him as well, he relates it to how Cham regularly has fal and fëlej, though in this case as he notes it is much harder to explain (ː 203, 298, 350, 366) -- perhaps some influence from fëlej even? TODO may need reconsideration, testing vjej below.
w ˌɑ l ˈeː n i oː , v j ˈɛ j $verb: to need. Orel 1998 : 511. Relation to vlej?? Alt form vëjej?  Orel 1998: 511. 
w ˈɑ l l i s , v ˈa l $valley, only in phrase "mal e val" 'mountain and valley'. Also a toponym (in Mat, for example) -- Bonnet 388. Why no affectation of a > e ? Orel 1998:  493. Bonnet 388. 
w ˌɑ l ˈoː r e m , v l ˈɛ ɾ ə $value. Absent from Orel 1998 and Bonnet 1998; in Vatasescu 1997 (:447) it (and Romanian valoare) are treated as derivations off of the verb VALERE. This is now a PROPOSAL. 
w ˈɑ p ɑ , v ˈa p ə $heat. Rom *vapa but could instead be Old Italian vapa "vapor" -- Orel 1998: 49. TODO reexamine, might be native. 
w ˌe h ˈi k u l u m , v ˈɛ ɡ ə l $ear of vessel. Orel 1998: 497-8. Reexamine.
w ˌe h ˈi k u l u m , v ˈɛ ɟ ə $ear of vessel. Orel 1998: 497-8. Variants vjegë, vegë. Unclear. TODO reexamine.
w ˌeː k t ˈuː r ɑ m , v ɛ t ˈy ɾ ə $car. Lack of double rr /r/ is unsuspiciousː cf detyrë, gjymtyrë, fytyrë, natyrë, shëmbëlltyrë, yndyrë. 
w ˌeː l ˈɑː t i oː , v l ˈɛ s ə $betrothal, engagement. Vatasescu p118.
w ˈeː l u m , v ˈɛ l $veil, transparent cloth of fine fibers (Newmark 1998: 913). Not in Orel 1998, nor Bonnet 1998.  Attributed to Latin vēlum, but this may make more sense (with the single l in mind) as a loan from Old French veil and Occitan vel. May need to reexamine -- or attribute to Angevin, cf. Marr 2023. 
w ˌe n ˈeː n ɑ m , v ɾ ˈɛ ɾ ə $poison. Masculine; ə may be inserted and it may be nonetheless from venenum, not venenam (venenum was what existed in Latin). Gheg: vënen. Old Tosk attested: vëner. This may in fact be a Gheg loan into Tosk, making vler "bile" a doublet. Orel 1998: 514. Bonnet 388.
w ˌe n ˈeː n u m , v ə ɾ ˈɛ ɾ $bile, gall, venom. As vrer -- Orel 2000: 31, 54, 56. De Vaan 2017: 1735.-- as vërer
w ˈe n i oː , v ˈi j $verb: to come. Camarda; Orel 1998: 508. Bonnet 1998: 298. Matasovic 2024: 68
w ˌe n t i l ˈɑː n i oː , f t i lˠ ˈɔ j $verb: to make clear, set in order, explain. Orel 1998: 105. 
w ˈeː r ɑ , v ˈɛ ɾ ə $summer. Orel 1998: 499-500. 
w ˌeː r i t ˈɑː t e m , v ə ɾ t ˈɛ t $true. Modern vërtetë's ə likely inserted as it is an adjective -- indeed listed without it in Bonnet 1998:388. Orel 1998: 505. 
w ˌe r r ˈi k u l u m , v ɾ ˈi ɡ u lˠ $flap, lobe. Orel 2000: 54. Orel 1998: 516. 
w ˈe r s ɑ m , v j ˈɛ ɾ ʃ ə $poem. Orel 2000: 54. May just be gender shifted and from versum.
w ˌe r s ˈɑː n i oː , v ə ɾ ʃ ˈɔ j $verb: to gush. Orel 1998: 505. Bonnet 388. 
w ˌe s k ˈo n i oː , u ʃ c ˈɛ j $verb: to feed. Orel 1998: 490 (has it from passive Latin vescor). De Vaan 2017: 1733. Bonnet 1998: 388 as uescere. 
w ˈeː s k u m , v ˈɛ ʃ k $verb: to make withered. Latin vēscus "small, thin, weak". Adjective form once veshk also, now veshkët. Orel 1998: 502.  
w ˌeː s s ˈiː k ɑ m , f ʃ ˈi k ə $bladder, blister, cocoon. Cf Aromanian bishică, Romanian bășică , French vessie etc-- clearly the double -ss- is what existed in Proto-Romance here. Orel 2000(ː34) lists the Latin source as vēsīca, as does Bonnet 1998(:388), who also notes the variant mëshikë, which is handled in a separate entry below 
w ˌeː n s ˈiː k ɑ m , m ə ʃ ˈi k ə $bubble, blister, bladder. Regular per Orel 2000: 55. Orel 1998: 264. Likewise, De Vaan 2017: 1739, citing Orel 2000 p55. Vatasescu 1997(: 34, 195) notes variants including mëshikë, fshikë, pshikë, mpshikë and mbshikë. However, not a single Romance reflex of vēs(s)īca attests an -n- in the first syllable (REW p709 number 9276), so a new PROPOSED alternative is considered below: invēssīca. 
ˌi n w eː s s ˈiː k ɑ m , m ə ʃ ˈi k ə $bubble, blister, bladder. See above. 
w ˌe s t i ɡ ˈɑː n i oː , v ə ʒ ɡ ˈɔ j $verb: to monitor. Orel 1998: 506. Bonnet 388(*) as veSHgoj -- perhaps reexamine. Lat inf vestigāre.  Matasovic 2024: 68 as vëzgoj. 
w ˈe s t i oː , v ˈɛ ʃ $verb: to get dressed. Vatasescu 1998: 87. 
w ˈe t e r e m , v j ˈɛ t ə ɾ $old. Orel 2000: 54, Vatasecsu 1997: 19. An alternative hypothesis attributes it to a derivation off of "vjet" (year). Orel 1998: 512. De Vaan 2017: 1735. Bonnet 388 (as vetus-- but acc is veterum). 
w ˈi ɑ , v ˈi j ə $line, stripe, crease. Orel 1998: 508. Bonnet 388. 
w ˌi ɡ ˈi l i ɑ m , v ə ɟ ˈi l ɛ $evening before a holiday. Vatasescu 1997(: 473)--  Also Tosk vëngjille with apparent n-inlaut, and Old Gheg mëngjille, modern Gheg mnjille and mjille. 
w ˈi k i ɑ , v ˈi c ə $vetch. Form unattested > unattested *vigjë through hypercorrection (why?) >> vigjëz with lexicalized suffixation. Cf Orel 1998: 508. Reexamine, possibly remove...
w ˌiː k ˈiː n u m , f c ˈi ɲ $neighbor. Orel 1998: 102. De Vaan 2017: 1736 as Gheg fqī. Bonnet 388. 
w ˌi k t ˈo r i ɑ , v i t ˈɔ ɾ ɛ $mythical serpent. Orel 2000: 117. Orel 1998: 510. However, there may be another etymology in `spinster' from an earlier word of the shape of ~vektore (Cabej 1968 apud Albert Doja, 2005, Anthropos, "Mythology and Destiny").
w ˌi k t u ˈɑː l i ɑ , v i ɟ ˈɛ $wedding gift, dinner on the third day after the child's birth. Orel 2000: 114. Inherited form vigjé but now vigjë, hypercorrection from pattern of forming singulativized plurals? Orel 1998: 506 -- "The sonoration of the dental may point to the late date of borrowing". Reexamine. 
w ˈi l l ɑ , v ˈi l ə $toponym. Lura (western Kukes county). Bonnet 388. 
w ˌiː l l ˈɑː n e ɑ , v lˠ ˈa ɲ ə $garden-bed, plot. Orel 1998: 513. 
w ˌi n ɡ ˈi l i ɑ , m ə ɲ ɟ ˈi lˠ $vigil, fast. Regular as mënjill per Orel 2000: 55. As vigilia > vëngjill/mëngjill in De Vaan 2017: 1739. Vatasescu 1997(:473) lists a *Gheg* mnjille reflecting Old Albanian (including Old Gheg, in Bogdani) mëngjille, as well as a mjille "ajunul unei sărbători”, corresponding to a Tosk vëgjile and vëngjille. Currently using mëngjill as it seems to be the center of gravity (of sources examined thus far), and of course ɲɟ > ɲ would be the regular Gheg ND > N shift. It appears that in the REW (p712), nasals in the first syllable of Latin etyma in vigil- are unattested in Romance. Alternate PROPOSED etymology in invigilia considered below. Bonnet 1998(: 192) lists mëngjille, mnjille, vëngjille considers this to reflect Latin vigilia, with an analogical nasal under the influence of evangelium > ungjill "gospel" (perhaps also angelu > ëngjëll "angel"?); on p198 he remarks on this as one of six cases where a non-palatal lateral reflects /lj/. TODO Reexamine -- need to check Bonnet, and form in Newmark -- consider removal. 
ˌi n w i ɡ ˈi l i ɑ , m ə ɲ ɟ ˈi lˠ $vigil, fast. See above. 
w ˈi r ɡ i n e m , v ˈi ɾ ɟ ə ɾ $maiden. Gheg: virgjin -- Orel 2000: 28. In Buzuku -- virgjënë (Vatasescu 1997: 20). Orel 1998: 509. Vatasescu 1997(:20) gives the Tosk form as vërgjërë instead, Landi 1989(:57) gives a virgjë. Per Vatasescu 1997(:20), Aromanian virghinë and virghirë are Alb. loans. 
w ˌi r ɡ ˈɑː n e m , v ˈa ɾ ɡ ə ɾ $uncastrated ram. Tosk also has vërgër. Gheg: vërgâ. Orel 1998: 495. See also Vatasescu 1997(:205).
w ˈi r i d ɑ m , v j ˈɛ ɾ ð ə $toponym,  near Shkoder. Bonnet 1998(: 73) ~ based on viridis, case of unexpected (for him) diphthongisation.
w ˈi r i d e m , v ˈɛ ɾ ð ə $yellow, or light green. Orel 2000: 105. Final ə may have been added as it is an adjective. De Vaan 2017: 1735. Bonnet 1998(:388) as with -ë. 
w ˌi r t ˈuː t e m , v ə ɾ t ˈy t $virtue. Inherited form seems to be vërtyt, the attested Old Alb form -- with the i in the first syll found in most dialects (as virtyt) may be influence by Latin in middle ages(?). Orel 1998: 505. Bonnet 1998: 88, 292. Buzuku vërtude, vërtudja (Vatasescu 1997 p62). Matasovic 2024: 69.
w ˌi s i t ˈɑː n i oː , v ə ʃ t ˈɔ j $verb: to see, watch. More common variant: vështroj. Orel 1998: 506; Vatasescu 1997: 40.
w ˈi s t u l u m , v ˈɛ ʃ t u lˠ $mistletoe. Vatasescu 1997(:188), Bonnet 1998(:124, 245).
w ˈi s k u m , v ˈɛ ʃ k $mistletoe. = Romanian vâsc, and cognates in Old Italian, Sardinian, oïl, Catalan, Provençal. Vatasescu 1997: 188. 
w ˈi t i u m , v ˈɛ s $vice. Orel 2000(:28-9) attributes it to "later layer of Latin loanwords" when short e reappeared. But may instead by Occitan vetz, Italian vezzo or Sicilian vezzu...? Orel 1998: 501. De Vaan 2017: 1744.
w ˌi t ˈu l e ɑ , f t ˈu j ə $one-year old she-goat. Variants: vëtulë, ftulë. Orel 1998: 15. Vatasescu 1997(: 205) on more discussion -- Old Albanian has fëtujë (Brâncus̩ 1973: 292-3 apud Vatasescu), there is also a "vetul" (Totoni 1964 teil II : p135 apud Vatasescu 1997); may be autochton alas -- see discussion in Vatasescu. Cf. Romanian vătui and vătuie, Aromanian vitul'ǔ (masc) and vitul'ě (fem.) -- Densusianu 1928 II 465 apud Vatasescu. 
w ˈiː t r i k u s , v ˈi t ə ɾ k $stepfather (archaic). In Vlorë: vitruk, vitkur. Cf Romanian vitreg. Orel 1998: 509. Bonnet 1998: 388. 
w ˌi t t ˈu l ɑ , v ɛ t ˈu lˠ ə $eyebrow, overhang. Orel 1998: 503. Vatasescu 1997: 27. Some others attribute it to Romance vitulla but this would be vetulë not vetullë, and the -tt- is supported by Latin vitta "band". 
w ˌiː w ˈo n i oː , v ˈu a̯ j $verb: to suffer. Latin "live" -> "survive" -> "suffer" (how depressingǃ). Orel 1998: 516-7. Lat verb was vīvō, vīvere. 
w ˈo l ɑ , v ˈa lˠ ə $sorb-apple. Romance *vola < Latin volāre "to fly" per Orel 1998(:494). Seems questioniable. Gheg form vollë. Phonology seems *maybe* plausible but the semantics dubious here. 
w ˈo l p u l u m , v ˈɔ l p u lˠ  $placename, "little fox". Bonnet 1998: 78, 236. Maja Volpul in Tropoja also -- Vatasescu 1997(: 208). Jokl (1928: 204) considered Maja Volpul at least a more recent loan. 
w ˌo l u n t ˈɑː t e m , v u lˠ n ˈɛ t $will. Orel 2000: 54. Orel 1998: 517. vullëndet in Buzuku -- De Vaan 2017: 1737. Bonnet 1998: 388. 
w ˈoː m i s , ˈu m b $ploughshare. Orel 2000: 56. Bonnet 1998: 81, 388. De Vaan 2017: 1735 as from "vomer", reexamine? Orel 1998(:485) marks this as a Gheg item, wiht other forms being um and hum, and argues it comes specifically from the Latin nominative vōmis. 
w ˌu l n e r ˈɑː t ɑ , v u r ˈa t ə $scar, mark, brand. Orel 1998: 517.
